<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br/>
<span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://ar2015.bertelsmann.com" rel="nofollow">Annual Report 2015</a></span></td>

<p><b>Bertelsmann</b> is a German <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> based in <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCtersloh" title="Gütersloh">Gütersloh</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. It is one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">mass media</a> companies and also active in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_sector" title="Service sector">service sector</a> and <a href="/wiki/Educational_technology" title="Educational technology">education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Bertelsmann was founded as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publishing_house" title="Publishing house">publishing house</a> by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Bertelsmann" title="Carl Bertelsmann">Carl Bertelsmann</a> in 1835.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Bertelsmann, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Mohn" title="Reinhard Mohn">Reinhard Mohn</a>, went from being a medium-sized enterprise to a major conglomerate, offering not only books but also television, radio, magazines and business services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Bertelsmann is an unlisted and <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital market</a>-oriented company,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> which remains primarily controlled by the Mohn family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Since 2016, major divisions of Bertelsmann are <a href="/wiki/RTL_Group" title="RTL Group">RTL Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Random_House" title="Penguin Random House">Penguin Random House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gruner_%2B_Jahr" title="Gruner + Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMG_Rights_Management" title="BMG Rights Management">BMG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arvato" title="Arvato">Arvato</a>, Bertelsmann Printing Group, Bertelsmann Education Group and Bertelsmann Investments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1835_to_1944">1835 to 1944</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1835 to 1944">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="551" data-file-width="600" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg/220px-Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg/330px-Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg/440px-Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bertelsmann-Signet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
first logo of C. Bertelsmann (2012)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The nucleus of the corporation is the <i>C. Bertelsmann Verlag</i>, a publishing house established in 1835 by Carl Bertelsmann in Gütersloh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Carl Bertelsmann was a representative of the "<a href="/wiki/Minden-Ravensberg" title="Minden-Ravensberg">Minden-Ravensberger</a> Erweckungsbewegung", a <a href="/wiki/Christian_revival" title="Christian revival">Protestant revival</a> movement, whose writings he published.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The C. Bertelsmann Verlag, originally specialized in theological literature, expanded its publications to include school and textbooks, and in the 1920s and 1930s increasingly entered into the field of light fiction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>, the publishing house gained a prominent position with its affordable "Bertelsmann Volksausgaben" ("people's editions").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In particular, war adventure books such as Werner von Langsdorff's "Fliegerbuch" on aviation were a commercial success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Heinrich Mohn belonged to the patrons' circle of the paramilitary <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">Schutzstaffel</a> organization and sought to turn his company into a National Socialist model enterprise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the C. Bertelsmann Verlag became a leading supplier to the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> even surpassing the central publishing house of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">NSDAP</a> <a href="/wiki/Franz_Eher_Nachfolger" title="Franz Eher Nachfolger">Franz Eher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Especially in the years between 1939 and 1941, the revenues of the C. Bertelsmann Verlag skyrocketed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Jewish slave laborers were not forced to work in Gütersloh, but in printing plants in <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> with which the C. Bertelsmann Verlag cooperated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1944, the <a href="/wiki/Reichskulturkammer" title="Reichskulturkammer">Reichsschrifttumskammer</a> (Reich Chamber of Literature) closed the publishing house to "mobilize all powers for victory".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Another essential reason for this was criminal paper racketeering by some publisher's employees,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> which led to a <a href="/wiki/Legal_proceeding" title="Legal proceeding">trial</a> in 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1945_to_1970">1945 to 1970</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1945 to 1970">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After World War II, the company portrayed itself to the Allied Control Authority as a Christian publisher that was part of the <a href="/wiki/German_resistance_to_Nazism" title="German resistance to Nazism">resistance to Nazism</a> and allegedly persecuted. Ties to National Socialist organizations were initially denied. After it became known that erroneous, or at least inadequate, statements had been made, Heinrich Mohn stepped down as the head of the publishing house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Mohn" title="Reinhard Mohn">Reinhard Mohn</a>, one of his three sons, took over the C. Bertelsmann Verlag, as Hans Heinrich Mohn had been killed in the war and Sigbert Mohn was still a prisoner of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In 1947, the Allies finally granted the company a publishing license.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> After the currency reform in 1948, there was a market slump in the book trade that also led to the next existential crisis for the C. Bertelsmann Verlag.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Under these conditions, in 1950 Bertelsmann launched the Lesering (book club) to stimulate sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The customers ordered books via subscription, and in return, received discounted prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The business increasingly shifted from the publishing house to the sale of books, which was decisive to further growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1959, the C. Bertelsmann Verlag was restructured: From that point on, theological literature was published in the <i>Gütersloher Verlagshaus</i>, a new publishing house which was consolidated with the <i>Rufer Verlag</i>. Fiction, poetry and art came under the roof of <i>Sigbert Mohn Verlag</i>. The C. Bertelsmann Verlag focused on nonfiction books, in particular dictionaries, guidebooks, reference books and journals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The 1950s and 1960s, Bertelsmann expanded its activities into new business areas: Thus, 1956, the company entered the music market with the Bertelsmann Schallplattenring (record club). Two years later, Ariola, one of the most successful German record labels was launched,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> and virtually at the same time, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonopress" title="Sonopress">Sonopress</a> record pressing plant was established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> With the <i>Kommissionshaus Buch &amp; Ton</i> (book and audio commissioning company), from which the <i>Vereinigte Verlagsauslieferung</i> (VVA) emerged, Bertelsmann laid the cornerstone for its service business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1964, Bertelsmann purchases the already broken-up <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universum_Film_AG" title="Universum Film AG">UFA</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> and built on its presence in cinema and television.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In 1969, Bertelsmann acquired shares in the magazine publisher <a href="/wiki/Gruner_%2B_Jahr" title="Gruner + Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</a>. A merger with <a href="/wiki/Axel_Springer_SE" title="Axel Springer SE">Axel Springer</a>, also planned at the time, for which a loan for millions had been taken out temporarily from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westdeutsche_Landesbank" title="Westdeutsche Landesbank">Westdeutsche Landesbank</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> failed in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1971_to_1983">1971 to 1983</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1971 to 1983">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2598" data-file-width="1998" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg/170px-Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg/255px-Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg/340px-Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reinhard_Mohn_Portrait_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Mohn" title="Reinhard Mohn">Reinhard Mohn</a> (2008)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1971, Bertelsmann operated as a <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Aktiengesellschaft" title="Aktiengesellschaft">Aktiengesellschaft</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The increasingly diversifying book publishers were bundled in the <i>Verlagsgruppe Bertelsmann</i> publishing group at the end of the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In 1972, this company moved from Gütersloh to Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Key divisions remained in Gütersloh, for which a new office building was built in 1976 at the Group's official location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> To this day, it has remained the Bertelsmann headquarters, referred to as the <i>Bertelsmann Corporate Center</i>. The rapid growth of Bertelsmann led to structural and financial problems. In the 1970s, financing requirements reached their peak. From 1975 to 1980, for example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Return_on_sales" title="Return on sales">return on sales</a> fell below one percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Bertelsmann also encountered new regulatory rules in its home market, in particular through laws governing mergers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Larger acquisitions became practically impossible. At the same time, there was an increasing saturation of the German market for the Bertelsmann Lesering,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> whereas the foreign book clubs earned the lion's share of revenues in this corporate division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The internationalization of Bertelsmann, initiated in the 1960s, was taken further:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Among other things, Bertelsmann acquired shares in the publishing houses Plaza &amp; Janés<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> based in Barcelona and <a href="/wiki/Bantam_Books" title="Bantam Books">Bantam Books</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> from New York City. In the United States, a location was established for <a href="/wiki/Ariola_Records" title="Ariola Records">Ariola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista Records</a> was acquired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In the period of the <a href="/wiki/Early_1980s_recession" title="Early 1980s recession">1979–1980 recession</a>, there was discussion concerning the succession of Reinhard Mohn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In 1981, he finally moved over to the <a href="/wiki/Supervisory_board" title="Supervisory board">supervisory board</a>. Manfred Fischer, who had previously headed up management of Gruner + Jahr, became the new <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chairman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> With this move, Bertelsmann, for the first time, was led by a manager who was not a member of the owner family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Mark Wössner became Fischer's successor as chairman and chief executive officer of Bertelsmann in 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The affair concerning the forged <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Diaries" title="Hitler Diaries">Hitler diaries</a> occurred at the beginning of his tenure, which damaged the reputation of Gruner + Jahr and Bertelsmann as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1984_to_1993">1984 to 1993</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1984 to 1993">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mark Wössner brought the subsidiaries closer to headquarters in Gütersloh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In particular, this involved business development and controlling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Under the leadership of Mark Wössner, Bertelsmann also took a stake in <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" title="RTL Television">RTL plus</a>, the first private TV broadcaster in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In 1986, Bertelsmann acquired a majority in <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a> and merged its activities in the music market with the new <i>Bertelsmann Music Group</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonopress" title="Sonopress">Sonopress</a>, a company established in 1958 to manufacture records, was not part of the Bertelsmann Music Group, rather it was assigned to the print and industrial division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/Doubleday_(publisher)" title="Doubleday (publisher)">Doubleday</a>, another well-known publishing house was acquired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> As a result, the Group ascended to become a well-known international company, and Bertelsmann was temporarily the world's largest media group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bertelsmann_SE_.26_Co._KGaA_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bertelsmann_SE_.26_Co._KGaA-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_year" title="Financial year">financial year</a> of 1990/1991, Bertelsmann had over 45,000 employees and reached sales of 14.5 billion <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">Deutsche Mark</a> annually. 63% involved business outside of Germany, and the United States was the most important foreign market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> and the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Bertelsmann also expanded to <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, as well as into <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> For example, in 1989 the first branch outlet of the <i>Club Bertelsmann</i> opened in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The later development of Bertelsmann in the 1990s was marked by the spread of the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> as a mass medium, as well as changes to the ownership structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In 1993, Reinhard Mohn transferred the majority of capital shares to the <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann_Foundation" title="Bertelsmann Foundation">Bertelsmann Foundation</a> and assumed its chairmanship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The foundation itself was financed by profits of the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1994_to_2000">1994 to 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1994 to 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1200" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg/170px-Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg/255px-Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg/340px-Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Penguin_Random_House_Tower_New_York_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Random_House_Tower" title="Random House Tower">Penguin Random House Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> (2005)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1994, Gruner + Jahr acquired the magazines of <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a>, whereby Bertelsmann once again expanded its presence in the most important foreign market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bertelsmann_SE_.26_Co._KGaA_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bertelsmann_SE_.26_Co._KGaA-67">[67]</a></sup> From 1995, there was a new business division of multimedia at Bertelsmann. Its centerpiece was <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL Europe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> a joint venture of America Online and Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Prior to that, Bertelsmann had already acquired a direct share in America Online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The multimedia division also included <i>mediaWays</i> and <i>Pixelpark</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 1997, UFA merged with <i>Compagnie Luxembourgeoise de Télédiffusion</i> (CLT) to become a joint entertainment group based in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> With CLT-UFA, Bertelsmann was able to decisively diversify its business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Middelhoff" title="Thomas Middelhoff">Thomas Middelhoff</a> succeeded Mark Wössner as Bertelsmann Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Thomas Middelhoff was already previously a member of the management board of the multimedia division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Mark Wössner joined the supervisory board of the company and also became Chairman of the Bertelsmann Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>This management change coincided with the takeover of <a href="/wiki/Random_House" title="Random House">Random House</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> With this, the group advanced to become the largest publishing group in the <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Random House was merged with <i>Bantam Doubleday Dell</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> and the global headquarters of all Bertelsmann publishing houses were relocated to New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In 1999, Bertelsmann acquired the publisher <a href="/wiki/Springer_Science%2BBusiness_Media" title="Springer Science+Business Media">Springer science media</a>, which, among other things, was the market leader for mathematics and physics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In the year 2000, Bertelsmann dissolved its joint venture with AOL Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The sale of the shares in the joint venture to America Online yielded billions to Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In the same year, Bertelsmann and <a href="/wiki/Pearson_PLC" title="Pearson PLC">Pearson</a> formed the <a href="/wiki/RTL_Group" title="RTL Group">RTL Group</a> from their TV subsidiaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Bertelsmann initially owned a minority in the company, and gradually built up its share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Later, Bertelsmann secured the majority of the shares in RTL through a share swap with the <a href="/wiki/Groupe_Bruxelles_Lambert" title="Groupe Bruxelles Lambert">Groupe Bruxelles Lambert</a> (GBL), which as a result owned 25.1% of Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2001_to_2007">2001 to 2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2001 to 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under the leadership of Thomas Middelhoff,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Bertelsmann increased its involvement in the Internet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> whereby above all the investment in <a href="/wiki/Napster" title="Napster">Napster</a> received major media attention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The aim of the acquisition, among other things,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> was to stem the illegal spread of copyrighted material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In 2001, the service nonetheless had to be shut down due to legal disputes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Bertelsmann faced several claims for damages by the music industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In order to finance additional growth of Bertelsmann, Thomas Middelhoff raised the idea of going public,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> which led to fundamental disagreement with the Mohn family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Gunter_Thielen" title="Gunter Thielen">Gunter Thielen</a> became the new Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of Bertelsmann,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and some members of the media viewed the change critically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>A consolidation phase followed, in order to solve the problems with the core business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> For example, Bertelsmann sold unprofitable e-commerce firms like the online shop of <a href="/wiki/Barnes_%26_Noble" title="Barnes &amp; Noble">Barnes &amp; Noble</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Gruner + Jahr sold the <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Zeitung" title="Berliner Zeitung">Berliner Zeitung</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and the scientific publisher, <i>BertelsmannSpringer</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> was spun off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> In the 2003 financial year, Bertelsmann announced that it was investing its music business in a <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Corporation" title="Sony Corporation">Sony</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Bertelsmann and Sony each owned half the shares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> With this transaction, the stakeholders sought to respond to declining sales in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_market" title="Music market">music market</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In addition, Gunter Thielen initiated the buyback of the shares from Groupe Bruxelles Lambert, so that the Mohn family regained complete control of Bertelsmann from 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> This measure was also financed with the sale of the music rights business to <a href="/wiki/Vivendi" title="Vivendi">Vivendi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> During the tenure of Gunter Thielen, the number of employees at Bertelsmann exceeded 100,000 for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_to_2016">2008 to 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2008 to 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="1077" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg/170px-Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg/255px-Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg/340px-Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Rabe_2015-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Rabe_(manager)" title="Thomas Rabe (manager)">Thomas Rabe</a>, Chairman and <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> since 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Hartmut_Ostrowski" title="Hartmut Ostrowski">Hartmut Ostrowski</a> was appointed Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Bertelsmann sold its shares of the record label <a href="/wiki/Sony_BMG" title="Sony BMG">Sony BMG</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and since then the company has operated under the name of <i>Sony Music Entertainment</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> In 2008, Bertelsmann acquired the rights to the <a href="/wiki/Brockhaus_Enzyklop%C3%A4die" title="Brockhaus Enzyklopädie">Brockhaus Encyclopedia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> and from that time on, this reference work was published by the <i>Wissen Media Verlag</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> At the end of 2011, Hartmut Ostrowski suddenly announced that he was leaving Bertelsmann for unspecified personal reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Since 2012, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Rabe_(manager)" title="Thomas Rabe (manager)">Thomas Rabe</a> has been Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> In 2013, Bertelsmann floated part of its shares in the RTL Group on the stock exchange,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> in order to finance additional growth from the proceeds of the sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> In the year 2013, <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Random_House" title="Penguin Random House">Penguin Random House</a> became the world's largest publishing company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gruner_%2B_Jahr" title="Gruner + Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</a> was taken over completely by Bertelsmann in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Furthermore, under the leadership of Thomas Rabe, Bertelsmann increasingly invested in the education sector:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> In 2014, for example, <i>Relias Learning</i> was acquired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The company belongs to the <i>Bertelsmann Education Group</i>, established in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2016, the printing business was bundled in the <i>Bertelsmann Printing Group</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The Club Bertelsmann was wound up,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> and individual distribution partners are taking legal action against it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions">Divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_Bertelsmann" title="List of assets owned by Bertelsmann">List of assets owned by Bertelsmann</a></div>
<p>Bertelsmann is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decentralized_organization" title="Decentralized organization">decentralized organization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> This means that the divisions largely work independently. The holding handles central tasks, in the field of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_finance" title="Corporate finance">corporate finance</a>, for example.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> In 2016, Bertelsmann introduced a new structure of eight divisions:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/RTL_Group" title="RTL Group">RTL Group</a> (television and radio), <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Random_House" title="Penguin Random House">Penguin Random House</a> (book publishing), <a href="/wiki/Gruner_%2B_Jahr" title="Gruner + Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</a> (magazines), <a href="/wiki/BMG_Rights_Management" title="BMG Rights Management">BMG</a> (music rights), <a href="/wiki/Arvato" title="Arvato">Arvato</a> (services), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann_Education_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bertelsmann Education Group (page does not exist)">Bertelsmann Education Group</a> (education), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann_Printing_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bertelsmann Printing Group (page does not exist)">Bertelsmann Printing Group</a> (printing) and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann_Investments&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bertelsmann Investments (page does not exist)">Bertelsmann Investments</a> (investments).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RTL_Group">RTL Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: RTL Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RTL_Group" title="RTL Group">RTL Group</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png" title="RTL Group logo"><img alt="RTL Group logo" data-file-height="246" data-file-width="394" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png/150px-RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png/225px-RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png/300px-RTL_Group_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>The RTL Group is one of the leading European entertainment providers, based in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> The company runs a commercial private television and radio channels in several countries, including <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" title="RTL Television">RTL</a> and <a href="/wiki/VOX_(TV_channel)" title="VOX (TV channel)">VOX</a> in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> In 2015, with the <i>RTL Digital Hub</i>, the company launched a dedicated unit for <a href="/wiki/Video_clip#On_the_Internet" title="Video clip">web videos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> In addition, production companies, such as <a href="/wiki/FremantleMedia" title="FremantleMedia">FremantleMedia</a>, are part of the RTL Group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> In January 1997, Bertelsmann merged the UFA film and television company with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compagnie_Luxembourgeoise_de_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9diffusion" title="Compagnie Luxembourgeoise de Télédiffusion">Compagnie Luxembourgeoise de Télédiffusion</a> (CLT). The merger of CLT-UFA with <i>Pearson TV</i> in the year 2000 marked the beginning of the RTL Group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The company is listed on the stock exchange and has been majority-owned by Bertelsmann since 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Following the sale of shares in 2013, the stake is 75.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> In 2015, the RTL Group had 12,258 employees, sales were <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>6.0 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Penguin_Random_House">Penguin Random House</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Penguin Random House">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Random_House" title="Penguin Random House">Penguin Random House</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png" title="Penguin Random House logo"><img alt="Penguin Random House logo" data-file-height="322" data-file-width="630" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png/150px-Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png/225px-Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png/300px-Penguin_Random_House_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>Penguin Random House is the world's largest book publishing company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> The company was created in 2013 through the merger of the publishing businesses of Bertelsmann and <a href="/wiki/Pearson_PLC" title="Pearson PLC">Pearson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> With the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Random_House" title="Random House">Random House</a> in 1998, Bertelsmann already became the largest book publisher in the <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> 250 publishing houses on five continents are part of the company, including Random House and <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Books" title="Penguin Books">Penguin Books</a>, but also <a href="/wiki/Doubleday_(publisher)" title="Doubleday (publisher)">Doubleday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_A._Knopf" title="Alfred A. Knopf">Knopf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viking_Press" title="Viking Press">Viking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The German <i>Verlagsgruppe Random House</i> (<a href="/wiki/Goldmann_(publisher)" title="Goldmann (publisher)">Goldmann</a>, Heyne and others), based in Munich, is not part of Penguin Random House,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> yet it does belong to the same division at Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Penguin Random House has its main headquarters in the <a href="/wiki/Random_House_Tower" title="Random House Tower">Penguin Random House Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Bertelsmann currently has a 53% stake in the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> In 2015, the company had 10,582 employees worldwide, achieving sales of €3.7 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gruner_.2B_Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Gruner + Jahr">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gruner_%2B_Jahr" title="Gruner + Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png" title="Gruner + Jahr logo"><img alt="Gruner + Jahr logo" data-file-height="278" data-file-width="394" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png/150px-Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png/225px-Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png/300px-Gruner_und_Jahr_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>Gruner + Jahr is an internationally operating magazine publisher based in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>. Its publications include <a href="/wiki/Brigitte_(magazine)" title="Brigitte (magazine)">Brigitte</a>, <a href="/wiki/GEO_(magazine)" title="GEO (magazine)">Geo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stern_(magazine)" title="Stern (magazine)">Stern</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> and the company also has a majority stake in <i>Motor Presse Stuttgart</i> and <i>Dresdner Druck- und Verlagshaus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> In 2015, Gruner + Jahr had a presence in 20 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> The businesses in the United States have been sold in the meantime,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> and in terms of revenue, Germany and France are the most important markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Bertelsmann has had a stake in Gruner + Jahr since 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Bertelsmann gradually purchased shares from Richard Gruner, <a href="/wiki/Gerd_Bucerius" title="Gerd Bucerius">Gerd Bucerius</a> and John Jahr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> In 1976, Bertelsmann held 74.9% of Gruner + Jahr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In 2014, Bertelsmann took over the company completely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2015, sales of Gruner + Jahr totaled €1.54 billion, with 13,245 employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-2"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BMG">BMG</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: BMG">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/BMG_Rights_Management" title="BMG Rights Management">BMG Rights Management</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BMG_Logo_2016.png" title="BMG logo"><img alt="BMG logo" data-file-height="148" data-file-width="551" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/BMG_Logo_2016.png/150px-BMG_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/BMG_Logo_2016.png/225px-BMG_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/BMG_Logo_2016.png/300px-BMG_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>BMG is a <a href="/wiki/Music_publisher_(popular_music)" title="Music publisher (popular music)">music publishing company</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>. The BMG catalog encompasses rights to works by artists such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A9line_Dion" title="Céline Dion">Céline Dion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronan_Keating" title="Ronan Keating">Ronan Keating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> In 2008, the company was created after the group divested from the music market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Following the sale of <a href="/wiki/Sony_BMG" title="Sony BMG">Sony BMG</a>, Bertelsmann had retained the rights to 200, mainly European, artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Kohlberg_Kravis_Roberts" title="Kohlberg Kravis Roberts">Kohlberg Kravis Roberts</a> came on board with BMG, retaining a 51% majority in the company, and Bertelsmann held 49%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Since 2013, BMG has once again become a fully owned subsidiary of Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> In 2016, BMG became a division of Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> In the 2015 financial year, BMG was still part of the <i>Corporate Investments</i> segment, which included, among others, the Bertelsmann Education Group. In 2015, all the companies in this segment together achieved €624 million and had 3,415 employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-3"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arvato">Arvato</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Arvato">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Arvato" title="Arvato">Arvato</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arvato_Logo_2016.png" title="Arvato logo"><img alt="Arvato logo" data-file-height="276" data-file-width="630" height="66" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Arvato_Logo_2016.png/150px-Arvato_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Arvato_Logo_2016.png/225px-Arvato_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Arvato_Logo_2016.png/300px-Arvato_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>Arvato is an international service provider. In its current form, the company originated in the year 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> At that time, the print and industry sectors at Bertelsmann were restructured, whereby services received a higher priority than the print and machinery sector back then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Since the 1950s, Bertelsmann has been an active service provider,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> delivering books for other publishing companies, for example.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> To this day, <i>Vereinigte Verlagsauslieferung</i> (VVA) has belonged to Arvato.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> What's more, today Arvato offers services, for example, in the areas of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Customer_Relationship_Management" title="Customer Relationship Management">Customer Relationship Management</a> (CRM), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supply_Chain_Management" title="Supply Chain Management">Supply Chain Management</a> (SCM) and finance, as well as <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> The main headquarters of Arvato is Gütersloh, and additional locations exist in 22 countries, including <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> In 2015, there were 72,457 people working for Arvato, and sales reached a volume of €4.8 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-4"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bertelsmann_Printing_Group">Bertelsmann Printing Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bertelsmann Printing Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png" title="Bertelsmann Printing Group logo"><img alt="Bertelsmann Printing Group logo" data-file-height="203" data-file-width="472" height="65" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png/150px-Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png/225px-Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png/300px-Bertelsmann_Printing_Group_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>In January 2016, Bertelsmann bundled its printing activities in <a href="/wiki/Digital_printing" title="Digital printing">digital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Offset_printing" title="Offset printing">offset</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rotogravure" title="Rotogravure">gravure</a> in the <i>Bertelsmann Printing Group</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> It is Europe's largest player in the industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The corporate group is located in Gütersloh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Bertelsmann Printing Group includes not only GGP Media, Mohn Media, Prinovis, Sonopress, Vogel Druck and several other companies, but also <i>Be Printers</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Be Printers is in turn a spin-off of Arvato, created in 2012, in order to consolidate the group's printing business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> The business has been under pressure for years due to declining print editions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In the 2015 financial year, Be Printers achieved revenues of €742 million and had 3,415 employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-5"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup> The Bertelsmann Printing Group has revenues of 1.7 billion Euros and a total of 9,000 members of staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bertelsmann_Education_Group">Bertelsmann Education Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Bertelsmann Education Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png" title="Bertelsmann Education Group logo"><img alt="Bertelsmann Education Group logo" data-file-height="162" data-file-width="630" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png/150px-Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png/225px-Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png/300px-Bertelsmann_Education_Group_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>The Bertelsmann Education Group is dedicated to the education sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> It was established in 2015 and has its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> It includes, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Alliant_International_University" title="Alliant International University">Alliant International University</a> and Relias Learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> The acquisition of Relias Learning in 2014 formed the cornerstone for the Bertelsmann Education Group and was the largest acquisition by Bertelsmann since the purchase of Random House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Based on the restructuring of all divisions, Bertelsmann has not yet reported any revenue and employee figures for the Bertelsmann Education Group in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Annual_report" title="Annual report">annual report</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-6"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup> According to media reports, revenues were between €200 and €300 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bertelsmann_Investments">Bertelsmann Investments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Bertelsmann Investments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png" title="Bertelsmann Investments logo"><img alt="Bertelsmann Investments logo" data-file-height="154" data-file-width="630" height="37" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png/150px-Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png/225px-Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png/300px-Bertelsmann_Investments_Logo_2016.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<p>This division bundles the startup investments of Bertelsmann. The main focus is on <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_Report_2015_168-7"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_Report_2015-168">[168]</a></sup> <i>Bertelsmann Digital Media Investments</i> is based in Gütersloh and since 2014 has concentrated mainly on the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> With <i>Bertelsmann Asia Investments</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> <i>Bertelsmann Brazil Investments</i> and <i>Bertelsmann India Investments</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> three additional funds exist that are active in the growth regions defined by the holding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Bertelsmann Investments holds equity positions in a total of over 100 <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup companies</a>, above all from the digital economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From 1971 to 2012, Bertelsmann was a <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint stock company</a> under German law (<a href="/wiki/Aktiengesellschaft" title="Aktiengesellschaft">Aktiengesellschaft</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> Subsequently, the company was transformed into a <a href="/wiki/Partnership_limited_by_shares" title="Partnership limited by shares">partnership limited by shares</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kommanditgesellschaft_auf_Aktien" title="Kommanditgesellschaft auf Aktien">Kommanditgesellschaft auf Aktien</a>). The general partner is a European stock corporation (<a href="/wiki/Societas_Europaea" title="Societas Europaea">Societas Europaea</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Bertelsmann's rationale for this move, among others, was the aim of opening up for investors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> thus enabling them to participate in the financing of additional growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> The media commented the change of the legal structure "the turn of an era",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> as it essentially also enables the company to go public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> This move was not ultimately implemented, however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> Today, Bertelsmann is a company active in <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital markets</a>, issuing <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a>, for example.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Since 2001, the company has prepared its financial statements according to <a href="/wiki/International_Financial_Reporting_Standards" title="International Financial Reporting Standards">International Financial Reporting Standards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new legal entity does not change any of the ownership of Bertelsmann.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> As early as the 1970s and 1980s, the Mohn family built up the <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann_Foundation" title="Bertelsmann Foundation">Bertelsmann Foundation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> which has owned the majority of shares in Bertelsmann since 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> In addition to social responsibility, tax considerations played a role in this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Moreover, this strategy was intended to preserve the continuity of the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> Today, according to Bertelsmann, the Mohn family holds 19.1% of the shares. The three foundations, Bertelsmann Foundation, Reinhard Mohn Foundation and BVG Foundation, together own 80.9%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The <i>Bertelsmann Verwaltungsgesellschaft mbH</i> (BVG) has key influence on the whole group: It bundles all the voting rights of the Mohn family and foundations with ownership shares. Together, they own 100 percent in the <a href="/wiki/Annual_general_meeting" title="Annual general meeting">general assemblies</a> of the group company (Bertelsmann SE &amp; Co. KGaA) and its general partner (Bertelsmann Management SE).</p>
<p>Bertelsmann SE &amp; Co. KGaA is managed by the Bertelsmann Management SE. The Chairman of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_board" title="Executive board">executive board</a> of Bertelsmann Management SE is Thomas Rabe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Other members of the executive board include Fernando Carro, Markus Dohle, Immanuel Hermreck, Bernd Hirsch and Anke Schäferkordt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> In 2012, Bertelsmann created the additional so-called <i>Group Management Committee</i>, in order to advise the executive board in important matters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> Some members of the media noted that a relatively large number of women have been appointed to the Group Management Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Bertelsmann SE &amp; Co. KGaA and Bertelsmann Management SE each have a <a href="/wiki/Supervisory_board" title="Supervisory board">supervisory board</a> that oversees the management. In 2013, Christoph Mohn assumed the chairmanship of both bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> From the family, <a href="/wiki/Liz_Mohn" title="Liz Mohn">Liz Mohn</a> and Brigitte Mohn are also members of the supervisory boards of both companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since the 1970s, the Bertelsmann headquarters have been in the Gütersloh district of Avenwedde, and its layout encompasses some 26,100 square meters. The office buildings were erected in 1976 and expanded in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> In addition to the typical facilities, the headquarters in Gütersloh also feature the <i>Bertelsmann University</i>, an academic institution for Bertelsmann executives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> In 1992, Bertelsmann purchased the <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann_Building" title="Bertelsmann Building">Bertelsmann Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and located its North American headquarters there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> The building was re-sold in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> The Berlin representative office was opened in 2003 in the <a href="/wiki/Alte_Kommandantur" title="Alte Kommandantur">Kommandantenhaus</a> in the historic center of Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> As part of international activities, Bertelsmann established additional locations at the corporate level (Corporate Centers) in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> (2006), <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a> (2012) and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> (2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>Worldwide, with all divisions, Bertelsmann has almost 350 locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> The majority are in Europe, where the Group earns the largest share of its revenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> Over the past years, the Group has increasingly focused on the newly industrialized nations of Brazil, China and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> In Brazil, efforts have been aimed at expanding activities above all in the field of education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> Bertelsmann has already been involved in China since 1992,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> and today all divisions are represented there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> In India, Bertelsmann is focused on growth in the <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> sector, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bertelsmann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the 1990s, critical questions arose as to the role of Bertelsmann in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> It was precipitated by a speech given by the Chairman and Chief Executive Officer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Middelhoff" title="Thomas Middelhoff">Thomas Middelhoff</a>, on the occasion of his receiving the <a href="/wiki/Vernon_A._Walters" title="Vernon A. Walters">Vernon A. Walters Award</a> 1998 in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> Thomas Middelhoff portrayed Bertelsmann as one of the few non-Jewish media companies shut down by the National Socialists because it allegedly published subversive literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> This interpretation was severely criticized, for example, by publicist Hersch Fischler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> The speech led to a broad public debate and ultimately in 1998 to the establishment of an independent historical commission (IHC) by the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> This was headed by <a href="/wiki/Saul_Friedl%C3%A4nder" title="Saul Friedländer">Saul Friedländer</a>, and additional members were Norbert Frei, Trutz Rendtorff and Reinhard Wittmann. The IHC presented an interim report in the year 2000 and issued a final report in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> It stated, for example, that the suggestion that the <i>C. Bertelsmann Verlag</i> mounted resistance against National Socialism was clearly not accurate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> The company's "shut-down as a publisher of the resistance" could not be proven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Volker_Ullrich" title="Volker Ullrich">Volker Ullrich</a> proclaimed in the weekly <a href="/wiki/Die_Zeit" title="Die Zeit">Die Zeit</a> that the notion of the company's being "a resistance publisher" was clearly baseless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> The files of the IHC have been publicly available in the company archives of Bertelsmann in Gütersloh since 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup></p>
